       4                 :            :  *        Routines to evaluate qualification and targetlist expressions

       6                 :            :  * Portions Copyright (c) 1996-2008, PostgreSQL Global Development Group

       9                 :            :  * IDENTIFICATION
      10                 :            :  *        $PostgreSQL: pgsql/src/backend/executor/execQual.c,v 1.226.2.4 2010/08/26 18:54:59 tgl Exp $
      11                 :            :  *
      12                 :            :  *-------------------------------------------------------------------------
      13                 :            :  */
      14                 :            : /*
      15                 :            :  *       INTERFACE ROUTINES
      16                 :            :  *              ExecEvalExpr    - (now a macro) evaluate an expression, return a datum
      17                 :            :  *              ExecEvalExprSwitchContext - same, but switch into eval memory context
      18                 :            :  *              ExecQual                - return true/false if qualification is satisfied
      19                 :            :  *              ExecProject             - form a new tuple by projecting the given tuple
      20                 :            :  *
      21                 :            :  *       NOTES
      22                 :            :  *              The more heavily used ExecEvalExpr routines, such as ExecEvalScalarVar,
      23                 :            :  *              are hotspots. Making these faster will speed up the entire system.
      24                 :            :  *
      25                 :            :  *              ExecProject() is used to make tuple projections.  Rather then
      26                 :            :  *              trying to speed it up, the execution plan should be pre-processed
      27                 :            :  *              to facilitate attribute sharing between nodes wherever possible,
      28                 :            :  *              instead of doing needless copying.      -cim 5/31/91
      29                 :            :  *
      30                 :            :  *              During expression evaluation, we check_stack_depth only in
      31                 :            :  *              ExecMakeFunctionResult (and substitute routines) rather than at every
      32                 :            :  *              single node.  This is a compromise that trades off precision of the
      33                 :            :  *              stack limit setting to gain speed.
      34                 :            :  */

     226                 :            : 
     227                 :            : 
     228                 :            : /* ----------------------------------------------------------------
     229                 :            :  *              ExecEvalExpr routines
     230                 :            :  *
     231                 :            :  *              Recursively evaluate a targetlist or qualification expression.
     232                 :            :  *
     233                 :            :  * Each of the following routines having the signature
     234                 :            :  *              Datum ExecEvalFoo(ExprState *expression,
     235                 :            :  *                                                ExprContext *econtext,
     236                 :            :  *                                                bool *isNull,
     237                 :            :  *                                                ExprDoneCond *isDone);
     238                 :            :  * is responsible for evaluating one type or subtype of ExprState node.
     239                 :            :  * They are normally called via the ExecEvalExpr macro, which makes use of
     240                 :            :  * the function pointer set up when the ExprState node was built by
     241                 :            :  * ExecInitExpr.  (In some cases, we change this pointer later to avoid
     242                 :            :  * re-executing one-time overhead.)
     243                 :            :  *
     244                 :            :  * Note: for notational simplicity we declare these functions as taking the
     245                 :            :  * specific type of ExprState that they work on.  This requires casting when
     246                 :            :  * assigning the function pointer in ExecInitExpr.      Be careful that the
     247                 :            :  * function signature is declared correctly, because the cast suppresses
     248                 :            :  * automatic checking!
     249                 :            :  *
     250                 :            :  *
     251                 :            :  * All these functions share this calling convention:
     252                 :            :  *
     253                 :            :  * Inputs:
     254                 :            :  *              expression: the expression state tree to evaluate
     255                 :            :  *              econtext: evaluation context information
     256                 :            :  *
     257                 :            :  * Outputs:
     258                 :            :  *              return value: Datum value of result
     259                 :            :  *              *isNull: set to TRUE if result is NULL (actual return value is
     260                 :            :  *                               meaningless if so); set to FALSE if non-null result
     261                 :            :  *              *isDone: set to indicator of set-result status
     262                 :            :  *
     263                 :            :  * A caller that can only accept a singleton (non-set) result should pass
     264                 :            :  * NULL for isDone; if the expression computes a set result then an error
     265                 :            :  * will be reported via ereport.  If the caller does pass an isDone pointer
     266                 :            :  * then *isDone is set to one of these three states:
     267                 :            :  *              ExprSingleResult                singleton result (not a set)
     268                 :            :  *              ExprMultipleResult              return value is one element of a set
     269                 :            :  *              ExprEndResult                   there are no more elements in the set
     270                 :            :  * When ExprMultipleResult is returned, the caller should invoke
     271                 :            :  * ExecEvalExpr() repeatedly until ExprEndResult is returned.  ExprEndResult
     272                 :            :  * is returned after the last real set element.  For convenience isNull will
     273                 :            :  * always be set TRUE when ExprEndResult is returned, but this should not be
     274                 :            :  * taken as indicating a NULL element of the set.  Note that these return
     275                 :            :  * conventions allow us to distinguish among a singleton NULL, a NULL element
     276                 :            :  * of a set, and an empty set.
     277                 :            :  *
     278                 :            :  * The caller should already have switched into the temporary memory
     279                 :            :  * context econtext->ecxt_per_tuple_memory.  The convenience entry point
     280                 :            :  * ExecEvalExprSwitchContext() is provided for callers who don't prefer to
     281                 :            :  * do the switch in an outer loop.      We do not do the switch in these routines
     282                 :            :  * because it'd be a waste of cycles during nested expression evaluation.
     283                 :            :  * ----------------------------------------------------------------
     284                 :            :  */
     285                 :            : 
     286                 :            : 
     287                 :            : /*----------
     288                 :            :  *        ExecEvalArrayRef
     289                 :            :  *
     290                 :            :  *         This function takes an ArrayRef and returns the extracted Datum
     291                 :            :  *         if it's a simple reference, or the modified array value if it's
     292                 :            :  *         an array assignment (i.e., array element or slice insertion).
     293                 :            :  *
     294                 :            :  * NOTE: if we get a NULL result from a subscript expression, we return NULL
     295                 :            :  * when it's an array reference, or raise an error when it's an assignment.
     296                 :            :  *
     297                 :            :  * NOTE: we deliberately refrain from applying DatumGetArrayTypeP() here,
     298                 :            :  * even though that might seem natural, because this code needs to support
     299                 :            :  * both varlena arrays and fixed-length array types.  DatumGetArrayTypeP()
     300                 :            :  * only works for the varlena kind.  The routines we call in arrayfuncs.c
     301                 :            :  * have to know the difference (that's what they need refattrlength for).
     302                 :            :  *----------
     303                 :            :  */
     304                 :            : static Datum
     305                 :            : ExecEvalArrayRef(ArrayRefExprState *astate,
     306                 :            :                                  ExprContext *econtext,
     307                 :            :                                  bool *isNull,
     308                 :            :                                  ExprDoneCond *isDone)
     309                 :            : {
     310                 :      26201 :         ArrayRef   *arrayRef = (ArrayRef *) astate->xprstate.expr;

    5182                 :            : }
    5183                 :            : 
    5184                 :            : 
    5185                 :            : /*
    5186                 :            :  * ExecInitExpr: prepare an expression tree for execution
    5187                 :            :  *
    5188                 :            :  * This function builds and returns an ExprState tree paralleling the given
    5189                 :            :  * Expr node tree.      The ExprState tree can then be handed to ExecEvalExpr
    5190                 :            :  * for execution.  Because the Expr tree itself is read-only as far as
    5191                 :            :  * ExecInitExpr and ExecEvalExpr are concerned, several different executions
    5192                 :            :  * of the same plan tree can occur concurrently.
    5193                 :            :  *
    5194                 :            :  * This must be called in a memory context that will last as long as repeated
    5195                 :            :  * executions of the expression are needed.  Typically the context will be
    5196                 :            :  * the same as the per-query context of the associated ExprContext.
    5197                 :            :  *
    5198                 :            :  * Any Aggref and SubPlan nodes found in the tree are added to the lists
    5199                 :            :  * of such nodes held by the parent PlanState.  Otherwise, we do very little
    5200                 :            :  * initialization here other than building the state-node tree.  Any nontrivial
    5201                 :            :  * work associated with initializing runtime info for a node should happen
    5202                 :            :  * during the first actual evaluation of that node.  (This policy lets us
    5203                 :            :  * avoid work if the node is never actually evaluated.)
    5204                 :            :  *
    5205                 :            :  * Note: there is no ExecEndExpr function; we assume that any resource
    5206                 :            :  * cleanup needed will be handled by just releasing the memory context
    5207                 :            :  * in which the state tree is built.  Functions that require additional
    5208                 :            :  * cleanup work can register a shutdown callback in the ExprContext.
    5209                 :            :  *
    5210                 :            :  *      'node' is the root of the expression tree to examine
    5211                 :            :  *      'parent' is the PlanState node that owns the expression.
    5212                 :            :  *
    5213                 :            :  * 'parent' may be NULL if we are preparing an expression that is not
    5214                 :            :  * associated with a plan tree.  (If so, it can't have aggs or subplans.)
    5215                 :            :  * This case should usually come through ExecPrepareExpr, not directly here.

    6091                 :            : 
    6092                 :            : /* ----------------------------------------------------------------
    6093                 :            :  *              ExecQual
    6094                 :            :  *
    6095                 :            :  *              Evaluates a conjunctive boolean expression (qual list) and
    6096                 :            :  *              returns true iff none of the subexpressions are false.
    6097                 :            :  *              (We also return true if the list is empty.)
    6098                 :            :  *
    6099                 :            :  *      If some of the subexpressions yield NULL but none yield FALSE,
    6100                 :            :  *      then the result of the conjunction is NULL (ie, unknown)
    6101                 :            :  *      according to three-valued boolean logic.  In this case,
    6102                 :            :  *      we return the value specified by the "resultForNull" parameter.
    6103                 :            :  *
    6104                 :            :  *      Callers evaluating WHERE clauses should pass resultForNull=FALSE,
    6105                 :            :  *      since SQL specifies that tuples with null WHERE results do not
    6106                 :            :  *      get selected.  On the other hand, callers evaluating constraint
    6107                 :            :  *      conditions should pass resultForNull=TRUE, since SQL also specifies
    6108                 :            :  *      that NULL constraint conditions are not failures.
    6109                 :            :  *
    6110                 :            :  *      NOTE: it would not be correct to use this routine to evaluate an
    6111                 :            :  *      AND subclause of a boolean expression; for that purpose, a NULL
    6112                 :            :  *      result must be returned as NULL so that it can be properly treated
    6113                 :            :  *      in the next higher operator (cf. ExecEvalAnd and ExecEvalOr).
    6114                 :            :  *      This routine is only used in contexts where a complete expression
    6115                 :            :  *      is being evaluated and we know that NULL can be treated the same
    6116                 :            :  *      as one boolean result or the other.
    6117                 :            :  *
    6118                 :            :  * ----------------------------------------------------------------
    6119                 :            :  */
    6120                 :            : bool
    6121                 :            : ExecQual(List *qual, ExprContext *econtext, bool resultForNull)
    6122                 :            : {
    6123                 :            :         bool            result;
    6124                 :            :         MemoryContext oldContext;
    6125                 :            :         ListCell   *l;
    6126                 :            :

    6140                 :            :          * Evaluate the qual conditions one at a time.  If we find a FALSE result,
    6141                 :            :          * we can stop evaluating and return FALSE --- the AND result must be
    6142                 :            :          * FALSE.  Also, if we find a NULL result when resultForNull is FALSE, we
